DomainOfApplicabilityStatus
^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^

.. raw:: html

  <table class="element-table">
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">IRI</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href='#DomainOfApplicabilityStatus' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('DomainOfApplicabilityStatus')){window.location.href='https://w3id.org/pink#DomainOfApplicabilityStatus'; return false;}">https://w3id.org/pink#DomainOfApplicabilityStatus</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-annotations" colspan="2">Annotations</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">prefLabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">DomainOfApplicabilityStatus</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">definition</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">A result of a model or software indicating whether an input is within the applicability domain of the model or software. Applicability domain refers to the range of conditions and limitations within which a model can be reliably applied. It is a critical factor in determining the accuracy and validity of a model, as it defines the scope of its predictions and identifies potential sources of uncertainty. The process of defining the applicability domain involves assessing the model's performance under different conditions and establishing the boundaries of its predictive capabilities.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">scope note</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">It should take one of the following values: pink:undefined; pink:outOfDomain; pink:inDomain.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Subclass Of</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href='#Property' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('Property')){window.location.href='https://w3id.org/pink#Property'; return false;}">Property</a></td>
  </tr>
  </table>

Matter
^^^^^^

.. raw:: html

  <table class="element-table">
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">IRI</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href='#Matter' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('Matter')){window.location.href='https://w3id.org/pink#Matter'; return false;}">https://w3id.org/pink#Matter</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-annotations" colspan="2">Annotations</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">prefLabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Matter</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">definition</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">An entity that possess mass and occupies volume.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">scope note</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">From the definition it follows that matter is an object with fermionic parts., The interpretation of the term "matter" is not univocal. Several concepts are labelled with this term, depending on the field of science. The concept mass is sometimes related to the term "matter", even if the former refers to a physical quantity (precisely defined by modern physics) while the latter is a type that qualifies a physical entity.<br>It is possible to identify more than one concept that can be reasonably labelled with the term "matter". For example, it is possible to label as matter only the entities that are made up of atoms. Or more generally, we can be more fine-grained and call "matter" the entities that are made up of protons, neutrons or electrons, so that we can call matter also a neutron radiation or a cathode ray.<br>A more fundamental approach taken here, considers matter as entities that are made of quarks and leptons, without excluding particles like the W and Z bosons that possess some mass, but are not fermions. This definition also include antimatter.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Subclass Of</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href='#Entity' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('Entity')){window.location.href='http://www.w3.org/ns/prov#Entity'; return false;}">Entity</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Subclasses</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href='#ChemicalEntity' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('ChemicalEntity')){window.location.href='https://w3id.org/emmo/hume#ChemicalEntity'; return false;}">ChemicalEntity</a>, <a href='#Substance' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('Substance')){window.location.href='https://w3id.org/emmo/hume#Substance'; return false;}">Substance</a></td>
  </tr>
  </table>

  </table>

  </tr>
  </table>

  </table>


.. admonition:: Example


   Newton's law of motion is a model for how a body will move when subjected to forces.
   A mouse can be seen as a model for a human (e.g. in medicine).
   An architectural floor plan is a model of a house.

  </tr>
  </table>

  </table>


.. admonition:: Example


   John yesterday is the cause of John today, is an example of temporal-like causality. The desk supporting my laptop is a space-like causality.

  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-annotations" colspan="2">Annotations</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">prefLabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">semiotical</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">definition</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The base of all semiotic relations.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">scope note</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Semiotic relations take part in a triadic semiotic meaning-making process, where an 'interpreter' connects a 'sign' (e.g. a property) to an entity (called 'referent')., The semiotic relations in the PINK Annotation Scheme are inspirred by EMMO, which in turn is based on the semiotic theory by Charles Sanders Peirce (1839-1914)., Semiotic relations can be seen as shortcuts that replaces a series of complex causal relations with a single relation.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Subproperty Of</span></td>

    <td class="element-table-value">The class of all catalogued resources, the Superclass of dcat:Dataset, dcat:DataService, dcat:Catalog and any other member of a dcat:Catalog. This class carries properties common to all catalogued resources, including datasets and data services. The instances of this class SHOULD be included in a catalog. The instances of this class SHOULD be included in a catalog. It is strongly recommended to use a more specific sub-class. When describing a resource which is not a dcat:Dataset or dcat:DataService, it is recommended to create a suitable sub-class of dcat:Resource, or use dcat:Resource with the dcterms:type property to indicate the specific type.</td>

ArtificialMaterial

.. raw:: html

  <table class="element-table">
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">IRI</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href='#ArtificialMaterial' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('ArtificialMaterial')){window.location.href='https://w3id.org/emmo/hume#ArtificialMaterial'; return false;}">https://w3id.org/emmo/hume#ArtificialMaterial</a></td>

  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">definition</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Any substance engineered or created by humans, often to mimic or improve upon natural materials.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">scope note</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Artificial materials are typically engineered through chemical synthesis from natural raw materials like oil or coal, resulting in polymers such as plastics, nylon, or polyester, designed for specific, enhanced properties like strength, durability, or moldability not found in nature.</td>

  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">definition</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">A standalone atom has direct part one 'nucleus' and one 'electron_cloud'.<br><br>An O 'atom' within an O₂ 'molecule' is an 'e-bonded_atom'.<br><br>In this material branch, H atom is a particular case, with respect to higher atomic number atoms, since as soon as it shares its electron it has no nucleus entangled electron cloud.<br><br>We cannot say that H₂ molecule has direct part two H atoms, but has direct part two H nucleus.</td>
  </tr>

    <td class="element-table-value">A chemical entity comprises the two different ways to represents matter: as single recognizable particle entity (molecular entity) and as a composition of particle entities (substance).<br><br>This distinction is not well assessed in actual chemical nomenclature, in which an element name refers to both the pure elemental substance or the atom.<br><br>In the EMMO we force the adoption of a more strict categorization based on mereotopology.<br><br>The class Material hosts the subclasses for which a substance can be identified without necessarily considering its nature of molecule/atom or substance (e.g. hydrocarbon is the class of both hydrocarbon molecules or gases).</td>
  </tr>

ContinuumSubstance
^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^

.. raw:: html

  <table class="element-table">
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">IRI</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href='#ContinuumSubstance' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('ContinuumSubstance')){window.location.href='https://w3id.org/emmo/hume#ContinuumSubstance'; return false;}">https://w3id.org/emmo/hume#ContinuumSubstance</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-annotations" colspan="2">Annotations</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">prefLabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">ContinuumSubstance</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">definition</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">A state that is a collection of sufficiently large number of other parts such that:<br>- it is the bearer of qualities that can exists only by the fact that it is a sum of parts<br>- the smallest partition dV of the state volume in which we are interested in, contains enough parts to be statistically consistent: n [#/m3] x dV [m3] >> 1</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">scope note</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">A continuum is made of a sufficient number of parts that it continues to exists as continuum individual even after the loss of one of them i.e. a continuum is a redundant., A continuum is not necessarily small (i.e. composed by the minimum amount of sates to fulfill the definition).<br><br>A single continuum individual can be the whole fluid in a pipe., A continuum is the bearer of properties that are generated by the interactions of parts such as viscosity and thermal or electrical conductivity.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Subclass Of</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href='#Substance' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('Substance')){window.location.href='https://w3id.org/emmo/hume#Substance'; return false;}">Substance</a></td>
  </tr>

  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">definition</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">A matter that is not a particulate matter and that does not fullfill the criteria of being a continuum substance.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">scope note</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Mesoscopic substances typically exist on a length scale between atoms and molecules and macroscopic (bulk) substances. They are typically in the range of some nanometers to about a micrometer and often exhibit unique physical properties due to their size and shape.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>

  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">prefLabel</span></td>

  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">definition</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Any constitutionally or isotopically distinct atom, molecule, ion, ion pair, radical, radical ion, complex, conformer etc., identifiable as a separately distinguishable entity that can undergo a chemical reaction.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">scope note</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Molecular entity is used as a general term for singular entities, irrespective of their nature, while chemical species stands for sets or ensembles of molecular entities.<br><br>Note that the name of a compound may refer to the respective molecular entity or to the chemical species,</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Subclass Of</span></td>

    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Subclasses</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href='#PolyAtomicEntity' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('PolyAtomicEntity')){window.location.href='https://w3id.org/emmo/hume#PolyAtomicEntity'; return false;}">PolyAtomicEntity</a>, <a href='#Molecule' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('Molecule')){window.location.href='https://w3id.org/emmo/hume#Molecule'; return false;}">Molecule</a>, <a href='#Atom' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('Atom')){window.location.href='https://w3id.org/emmo/hume#Atom'; return false;}">Atom</a>, <a href='#http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CHEBI_23367' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CHEBI_23367')){window.location.href='http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/CHEBI_23367'; return false;}">MolecularEntity</a></td>
  </tr>
  </table>

  </table>


.. admonition:: Example


   Hydrogen molecule is an adequate definition of a certain molecular entity for some purposes, whereas for others it is necessary to distinguish the electronic state and/or vibrational state and/or nuclear spin, etc. of the hydrogen molecule.

   Methane, may mean a single molecule of CH4 (molecular entity) or a molar amount, specified or not (chemical species), participating in a reaction. The degree of precision necessary to describe a molecular entity depends on the context.



.. raw:: html




Molecule
^^^^^^^^

.. raw:: html

  <table class="element-table">
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">IRI</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href='#Molecule' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('Molecule')){window.location.href='https://w3id.org/emmo/hume#Molecule'; return false;}">https://w3id.org/emmo/hume#Molecule</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-annotations" colspan="2">Annotations</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">prefLabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Molecule</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">definition</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">An atom-based state defined by an exact number of e-bonded atomic species and an electron cloud made of the shared electrons.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">scope note</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">An entity is called essential if removing one direct part will lead to a change in entity class.<br>An entity is called redundant if removing one direct part will not lead to a change in entity class., This definition states that this object is a non-periodic set of atoms or a set with a finite periodicity.<br>Removing an atom from the state will result in another type of atom_based state.<br>e.g. you cannot remove H from H₂0 without changing the molecule type (essential). However, you can remove a C from a nanotube (redundant). C60 fullerene is a molecule, since it has a finite periodicity and is made of a well defined number of atoms (essential). A C nanotube is not a molecule, since it has an infinite periodicity (redundant).</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Subclass Of</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href='#MolecularEntity' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('MolecularEntity')){window.location.href='https://w3id.org/emmo/hume#MolecularEntity'; return false;}">MolecularEntity</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Subclasses</span></td>

  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">scope note</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">In the physical sciences, a phase is a region of space (a thermodynamic system), throughout which all physical properties of a material are essentially uniform. Examples of physical properties include density, index of refraction, magnetization and chemical composition. A simple description is that a phase is a region of material that is chemically uniform, physically distinct, and (often) mechanically separable. In a system consisting of ice and water in a glass jar, the ice cubes are one phase, the water is a second phase, and the humid air is a third phase over the ice and water. The glass of the jar is another separate phase.<br><br>The term phase is sometimes used as a synonym for state of matter, but there can be several immiscible phases of the same state of matter. Also, the term phase is sometimes used to refer to a set of equilibrium states demarcated in terms of state variables such as pressure and temperature by a phase boundary on a phase diagram. Because phase boundaries relate to changes in the organization of matter, such as a change from liquid to solid or a more subtle change from one crystal structure to another, this latter usage is similar to the use of "phase" as a synonym for state of matter. However, the state of matter and phase diagram usages are not commensurate with the formal definition given above and the intended meaning must be determined in part from the context in which the term is used.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Subclass Of</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href='#ContinuumSubstance' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('ContinuumSubstance')){window.location.href='https://w3id.org/emmo/hume#ContinuumSubstance'; return false;}">ContinuumSubstance</a></td>
  </tr>
  </table>

  </table>

.. admonition:: Example


   A litre of water.

   A pen can be classified as a substance (although it has parts with different properties) since it can be identified as being solid.

   MODA and CHADA are diagrammatic representation of a simulation or a characterisation workflow.

  </table>


.. admonition:: Example


   A data based model is only a functional model, since it provide the same relations between the properties of the object (e.g., it can predict some properties as function of others) but is not considering the internal mechanisms (i.e., it can ignore the physics).

.. admonition:: Example


   Newton's law of motion is a model for how a body will move when subjected to forces.
   A mouse can be seen as a model for a human (e.g. in medicine).
   An architectural floor plan is a model of a house.

  </tr>
  <tr>

    <td class="element-table-value">QSARModel</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">definition</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">A mathematical model (often a statistical correlation) relating one or more quantitative parameters derived from chemical structure to a quantitative measure of a property or activity (e.g. related to physical-chemical properties, ecotoxicology, environmental fate and transport, and human health hazards). QSARs are quantitative models yielding a continuous or categorical result.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">scope note</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The aim of a QSAR model is typically to reduce time, monetary cost and needed animal testing., To facilitate practical application of (Q)SAR approaches in regulatory contexts by governments and industry and to improve their regulatory acceptance, the OECD (Q)SAR project has developed various outcomes such as the principles for the validation of (Q)SAR models, guidance documents as well as the QSAR Toolbox.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>
  </tr>

  </table>

  </table>


.. admonition:: Example


   A small scale replica of a plane tested in a wind gallery shares the same functionality in terms of aerodynamic behaviour of the bigger one.

   Pinocchio is a functional model of a boy since it imitates the external behaviour without having the internal biological structure of a human being (it is made of magic wood...).
